  4550  // ListFindings List findings.
  4551  // Get a list of findings. These include both misconfigurations and identity risks.
  4552  //
  4553  // **Note**: To filter and return only identity risks, add the following query parameter: `?filter[tags]=dd_rule_type:ciem`
  4554  //
  4555  // ### Filtering
  4556  //
  4557  // Filters can be applied by appending query parameters to the URL.
  4558  //
  4559  //   - Using a single filter: `?filter[attribute_key]=attribute_value`
  4560  //   - Chaining filters: `?filter[attribute_key]=attribute_value&filter[attribute_key]=attribute_value...`
  4561  //   - Filtering on tags: `?filter[tags]=tag_key:tag_value&filter[tags]=tag_key_2:tag_value_2`
  4562  //
  4563  // Here, `attribute_key` can be any of the filter keys described further below.
  4564  //
  4565  // Query parameters of type `integer` support comparison operators (`>`, `>=`, `<`, `<=`). This is particularly useful when filtering by `evaluation_changed_at` or `resource_discovery_timestamp`. For example: `?filter[evaluation_changed_at]=>20123123121`.
  4566  //
  4567  // You can also use the negation operator on strings. For example, use `filter[resource_type]=-aws*` to filter for any non-AWS resources.
  4568  //
  4569  // The operator must come after the equal sign. For example, to filter with the `>=` operator, add the operator after the equal sign: `filter[evaluation_changed_at]=>=1678809373257`.
  4570  //
  4571  // Query parameters must be only among the documented ones and with values of correct types. Duplicated query parameters (e.g. `filter[status]=low&filter[status]=info`) are not allowed.
  4572  //
  4573  // ### Additional extension fields
  4574  //
  4575  // Additional extension fields are available for some findings.
  4576  //
  4577  // The data is available when you include the query parameter `?detailed_findings=true` in the request.
  4578  //
  4579  // The following fields are available for findings:
  4580  // - `external_id`: The resource external ID related to the finding.
  4581  // - `description`: The description and remediation steps for the finding.
  4582  // - `datadog_link`: The Datadog relative link for the finding.
  4583  // - `ip_addresses`: The list of private IP addresses for the resource related to the finding.

  6578  // ListVulnerabilities List vulnerabilities.
  6579  // Get a list of vulnerabilities.
  6580  //
  6581  // ### Pagination
  6582  //
  6583  // Pagination is enabled by default in both `vulnerabilities` and `assets`. The size of the page varies depending on the endpoint and cannot be modified. To automate the request of the next page, you can use the links section in the response.
  6584  //
  6585  // This endpoint will return paginated responses. The pages are stored in the links section of the response:
  6586  //
  6587  // ```JSON
  6588  //
  6589  //	{
  6590  //	  "data": [...],
  6591  //	  "meta": {...},
  6592  //	  "links": {
  6593  //	    "self": "https://.../api/v2/security/vulnerabilities",
  6594  //	    "first": "https://.../api/v2/security/vulnerabilities?page[number]=1&page[token]=abc",
  6595  //	    "last": "https://.../api/v2/security/vulnerabilities?page[number]=43&page[token]=abc",
  6596  //	    "next": "https://.../api/v2/security/vulnerabilities?page[number]=2&page[token]=abc"
  6597  //	  }
  6598  //	}
  6599  //
  6600  // ```
  6601  //
  6602  // - `links.previous` is empty if the first page is requested.
  6603  // - `links.next` is empty if the last page is requested.
  6604  //
  6605  // #### Token
  6606  //
  6607  // Vulnerabilities can be created, updated or deleted at any point in time.
  6608  //
  6609  // Upon the first request, a token is created to ensure consistency across subsequent paginated requests.
  6610  //
  6611  // A token is valid only for 24 hours.
  6612  //
  6613  // #### First request
  6614  //
  6615  // We consider a request to be the first request when there is no `page[token]` parameter.
  6616  //
  6617  // The response of this first request contains the newly created token in the `links` section.
  6618  //
  6619  // This token can then be used in the subsequent paginated requests.
  6620  //
  6621  // *Note: The first request may take longer to complete than subsequent requests.*
  6622  //
  6623  // #### Subsequent requests
  6624  //
  6625  // Any request containing valid `page[token]` and `page[number]` parameters will be considered a subsequent request.
  6626  //
  6627  // If the `token` is invalid, a `404` response will be returned.
  6628  //
  6629  // If the page `number` is invalid, a `400` response will be returned.
  6630  //
  6631  // The returned `token` is valid for all requests in the pagination sequence. To send paginated requests in parallel, reuse the same `token` and change only the `page[number]` parameter.
  6632  //
  6633  // ### Filtering
  6634  //
  6635  // The request can include some filter parameters to filter the data to be retrieved. The format of the filter parameters follows the [JSON:API format](https://jsonapi.org/format/#fetching-filtering): `filter[$prop_name]`, where `prop_name` is the property name in the entity being filtered by.
  6636  //
  6637  // All filters can include multiple values, where data will be filtered with an OR clause: `filter[title]=Title1,Title2` will filter all vulnerabilities where title is equal to `Title1` OR `Title2`.
  6638  //
  6639  // String filters are case sensitive.
  6640  //
  6641  // Boolean filters accept `true` or `false` as values.
  6642  //
  6643  // Number filters must include an operator as a second filter input: `filter[$prop_name][$operator]`. For example, for the vulnerabilities endpoint: `filter[cvss.base.score][lte]=8`.
  6644  //
  6645  // Available operators are: `eq` (==), `lt` (<), `lte` (<=), `gt` (>) and `gte` (>=).
  6646  //
  6647  // ### Metadata
  6648  //
  6649  // Following [JSON:API format](https://jsonapi.org/format/#document-meta), object including non-standard meta-information.
  6650  //
  6651  // This endpoint includes the meta member in the response. For more details on each of the properties included in this section, check the endpoints response tables.
  6652  //
  6653  // ```JSON
  6654  //
  6655  //	{
  6656  //	  "data": [...],
  6657  //	  "meta": {
  6658  //	    "total": 1500,
  6659  //	    "count": 18732,
  6660  //	    "token": "some_token"
  6661  //	  },
  6662  //	  "links": {...}
  6663  //	}
  6664  //
  6665  // ```
  6666  // ### Extensions
